## Objective
Determine whether a given `Claim` is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided `Evidence` and your internal knowledge base.

## Input Format
- **Evidence**: A list of objects in the format `{'key': 'Entity Name', 'value': <integer>}`.
- **Claim**: A natural language sentence making an assertion about the entities.

## Critical Reasoning Guidelines

### 1. Interpretation of Evidence
- **Ignore the `value` field**: The integer in the `value` field (0, 1, 3, 4, etc.) is **metadata** (e.g., retrieval score, document ID, or frequency). **DO NOT** use it for mathematical comparisons (e.g., do not check if `0 < 1`) or treat it as a direct truth value for the claim.
- **Focus on Presence**: The only information to extract from the evidence is the **existence** of the entity names listed in the `key` field.

### 2. Verification Logic (Hybrid Approach)
You must perform a two-step verification process:

**Step A: Entity Grounding**
- Identify all specific entities (people, places, organizations, works) mentioned in the `Claim`.
- Check if these entities appear in the `Evidence` list (matching the `key` field).
- *Rule*: If the claim relies on an entity that is **missing** from the evidence, the claim is generally **NOT_SUPPORTED** because the evidence does not provide the necessary context.

**Step B: Fact Verification (Internal Knowledge)**
- If the entities are present in the evidence, use your **internal knowledge base** to verify the specific relationship or attribute asserted in the claim.
- **SUPPORTED** if:
    1. The relevant entities are present in the evidence.
    2. The relationship described (e.g., "X owns Y", "Z starred in W", "A is also known as B") is a **verifiable, well-known fact**.
- **NOT_SUPPORTED** if:
    1. The relationship described is **false** according to your knowledge.
    2. The relationship is **too specific or obscure** to be verified by general knowledge (e.g., specific administrative classifications like "county-controlled" that cannot be inferred from the name alone, even if the entity exists).
    3. The evidence fails to mention a critical entity required to make the claim true.

### 3. Decision Criteria Summary
- **SUPPORTED**: Evidence contains the entities + Internal Knowledge confirms the relationship is true.
- **NOT_SUPPORTED**: Evidence is missing entities OR Internal Knowledge confirms the relationship is false OR the relationship is too obscure to be confirmed by general knowledge given the limited evidence.

## Examples of Logic Application

- **Case 1 (Corporate Ownership)**:
  - Evidence: `Hindustan Zinc`, `Vedanta Resources`.
  - Claim: "Anil Agarwal owns the parent of Hindustan Zinc."
  - Logic: Entities present. Internal knowledge confirms Vedanta is the parent and Agarwal owns Vedanta. -> **SUPPORTED**.

- **Case 2 (Obscure Attribute)**:
  - Evidence: `Guiping`, `Hailin`.
  - Claim: "Both are county controlled cities."
  - Logic: Entities present. Internal knowledge cannot definitively confirm the specific "county controlled" status just from the names without external data. The evidence does not explicitly state this attribute. -> **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

- **Case 3 (Film/History)**:
  - Evidence: `Detroit (film)`, `1967 Detroit riot`, `Will Poulter`.
  - Claim: "The film is about the 1967 riot... Will Poulter starred in it."
  - Logic: Entities present. Internal knowledge confirms the film's subject and cast. -> **SUPPORTED**.
  *(Note: If the claim had been "The film is about the 1967 riot which is a fictional event," and the evidence listed the riot, the answer would be NOT_SUPPORTED because the internal knowledge knows the riot was real.)*

## Output Format
Provide a brief reasoning process following the steps above, followed by the final verdict in bold: **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

- **Claim**: A natural language sentence or paragraph making an assertion about the entities.

## Critical Guidelines for Reasoning

1.  **Entity Presence Check**:
    - Verify that all specific entities mentioned in the `Claim` are present in the `Evidence` list (matching the `key` field).
    - If a critical entity in the claim is missing from the evidence, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

2.  **Fact Verification (The Core Logic)**:
    - Once entities are confirmed present, use your internal knowledge to verify the **specific assertions** made in the claim about those entities.
    - **Strict Consistency**: The claim must be factually accurate in every detail.
      - *Example*: If the claim states "Entity X was in Location Y," but your knowledge confirms Entity X was actually in Location Z, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**, even if Entity X is present in the evidence.
      - *Example*: If the claim states "Person A created Role B," but Person A only *portrayed* Role B (and did not create it), the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
    - **Ambiguity**: If the claim makes an assertion that cannot be verified as true (e.g., obscure details not found in general knowledge or contradictory to known facts), the verdict is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

3.  **Handling the `value` Field**:
    - **NEVER** use the numerical `value` (0, 1, 2) to determine truth, counts, or comparisons.
    - Treat the presence of the entity in the list as the only signal from the evidence. The `value` is noise.

4.  **Final Verdict**:
    - If the entities are present AND all factual assertions in the claim are consistent with known reality: **SUPPORTED**.
    - If entities are missing OR any factual assertion is incorrect/contradictory: **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

## Output Format
- Provide a step-by-step reasoning process explaining how you checked the entities and verified the facts.
- **Crucial**: The response must end with a single line containing the verdict in the exact format:
  `Verdict: SUPPORTED`
  OR
  `Verdict: NOT_SUPPORTED`

## Examples of Logic Application

- **Scenario A (Contradictory Detail)**:
  - Evidence: `{'key': 'Edgar Ray Killen', ...}`
  - Claim: "Edgar Ray Killen was a KKK organizer in Appomattox."
  - Reasoning: Entity is present. However, internal knowledge confirms Edgar Ray Killen was an organizer in Mississippi (Neshoba County), not Appomattox (Virginia). The location detail is false.
  - Result: `Verdict: NOT_SUPPORTED`

- **Scenario B (Correct Fact)**:
  - Evidence: `{'key': 'The Silent World', ...}, {'key': 'Zeitgeist', ...}`
  - Claim: "The Silent World (1956) has fewer films than Zeitgeist." (Assuming internal knowledge confirms the film counts or the relationship is a known fact in the dataset context).
  - Reasoning: Entities present. The relationship described aligns with known facts (or the specific dataset logic implies this relationship is true for these entities).
  - Result: `Verdict: SUPPORTED`

- **Scenario C (Missing Entity)**:
  - Evidence: `{'key': 'Philip Skinner', ...}`
  - Claim: "Philip Skinner and John Doe are both actors."
  - Reasoning: "John Doe" is not in the evidence.
  - Result: `Verdict: NOT_SUPPORTED`

Iteration 7 [k=1]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task: Fact Verification with Entity-Based Evidence

## Objective
Determine whether a given `Claim` is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided `Evidence` and your internal knowledge base.

## Input Format
- **Evidence**: A list of JSON-like objects in the format `{'key': 'Entity Name', 'value': <integer>}`.
  - `key`: The name of an entity (e.g., a person, organization, location, or event).
  - `value`: An integer (0, 1, 2, 3, etc.).
- **Claim**: A natural language sentence or paragraph making one or more assertions about the relationships between the entities.

## Critical Guidelines for Reasoning

### 1. Interpretation of Evidence Values
- **IGNORE the numerical `value` field completely.**
  - The `value` (0, 1, 2, 3, etc.) is **metadata** (likely a retrieval confidence score, index, or frequency count).
  - **Do NOT** use the `value` to perform mathematical comparisons (e.g., "0 is less than 1"), boolean logic (e.g., "0 means false"), or count verification.
  - The **only** information to extract from the evidence is the **presence** of the entity name in the `key` field. If an entity is listed, treat it as "retrieved" and relevant to the context.

### 2. Verification Strategy (Hybrid Approach)
This task requires a **Hybrid Verification** approach:
1.  **Entity Matching**: Check if the specific entities mentioned in the `Claim` are present in the `Evidence` list.
    - If the claim mentions an entity that is **NOT** in the evidence list, the claim is likely **NOT_SUPPORTED** (as the evidence does not cover the topic).
    - If the claim mentions entities that **ARE** in the evidence list, proceed to Step 2.
2.  **Internal Knowledge Validation**:
    - Since the evidence only provides *names* (not facts), you must use your **internal knowledge** to verify the specific relationships, dates, locations, or attributes described in the `Claim`.
    - **SUPPORTED**: If the entities are present in the evidence AND the factual relationship described in the claim is **true** according to general knowledge (e.g., "Camair-Co took over Cameroon Airlines in 2008" is a known fact).
    - **NOT_SUPPORTED**: If the entities are present but the factual relationship is **false**, **unknown**, or **cannot be inferred** solely from the entity names (e.g., asserting a specific birth city or a specific building address that is not a widely known "famous fact" associated with the entity name).

### 3. Decision Logic
- **SUPPORTED**:
  - The claim's entities are found in the evidence.
  - The claim describes a relationship that is factually correct (verifiable via internal knowledge).
  - *Example*: If evidence lists "Camair-Co" and "Augustin Frédéric Kodock", and the claim states "Camair-Co took over the airline Kodock led in 2008", and this is historically true -> **SUPPORTED**.
- **NOT_SUPPORTED**:
  - The claim mentions an entity not found in the evidence.
  - The claim describes a relationship that is factually false.
  - The claim makes a specific attribute assertion (e.g., "born in X", "headquartered in Y") that cannot be confirmed as a standard fact for that entity, even if the entity is present.
  - *Example*: If evidence lists "Guiping" and "Hailin", but the claim asserts they are "county controlled cities" and this specific classification is not a verifiable general fact or is incorrect -> **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

## Output Format
- You must provide a step-by-step reasoning process analyzing the entities and the facts.
- **CRITICAL**: The final line of your response must be exactly one of the following two labels:
  - `SUPPORTED`
  - `NOT_SUPPORTED`
- Do not include any other text after the final label.

## Examples of Logic Application

**Scenario A (Success Case):**
- Evidence: `{'key': 'Camair-Co', 'value': 1}`, `{'key': 'Augustin Frédéric Kodock', 'value': 2}`
- Claim: "Camair-Co took over the airline that Augustin Frédéric Kodock was head of in March 2008."
- Reasoning: Both entities are present. Internal knowledge confirms Camair-Co was founded in March 2008 to replace Cameroon Airlines, which was led by Kodock. The facts align.
- Verdict: `SUPPORTED`

**Scenario B (Failure Case):**
- Evidence: `{'key': 'Guiping', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': 'Hailin', 'value': 0}`
- Claim: "Both are county controlled cities."
- Reasoning: Entities are present. However, the specific administrative status "county controlled city" is not a standard, verifiable fact derivable just from the names (unlike a famous event or a major corporate takeover). The evidence does not contain the attribute data, and internal knowledge does not confirm this specific classification as a primary fact for these names in this context.
- Verdict: `NOT_SUPPORTED`

Iteration 7 [k=2]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task: Claim Verification with Entity-Based Evidence

## Objective
Determine whether a given `Claim` is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided `Evidence` and your internal knowledge base.

## Input Format
- **Evidence**: A list of JSON-like objects in the format `{'key': 'Entity Name', 'value': <number>}`.
- **Claim**: A natural language sentence or paragraph making an assertion about the entities.

## Critical Guidelines for Reasoning

### 1. Interpretation of Evidence Data
- **Ignore Numerical Values**: The `value` field (e.g., 0, 1, 5) in the evidence objects is **metadata** (likely retrieval confidence scores, indices, or noise). **DO NOT** use these numbers for mathematical comparison (e.g., do not check if `0 < 1` or `5 > 1`).
- **Focus on Entity Presence**: The only relevant information in the evidence is the **presence of the entity name** (`key`). If an entity mentioned in the claim appears in the evidence list, it is considered "retrieved" and valid for verification.

### 2. Verification Strategy (The "Context + Knowledge" Logic)
This task requires a two-step verification process:
1.  **Entity Matching**: Check if the specific entities required to prove the claim are present in the `Evidence` list.
    - *Example*: If the claim mentions "Ermal C. Fraze" and "Kettering University", verify that both names appear in the evidence keys.
2.  **Fact Verification**: Once entities are confirmed present, use your **internal knowledge** to verify if the relationship or attribute described in the claim is factually true for those entities.
    - *Supported*: The entities are present in the evidence AND the claim describes a known, true fact about them (e.g., "X is the inventor of Y", "Z is a university").
    - *Not Supported*: The entities are present, but the claim makes an assertion that is false, or the specific attribute (e.g., "county controlled city") cannot be verified as a standard fact even with the entities present.

### 3. Handling Ambiguity
- If the claim relies on a specific attribute that is not a well-known, verifiable fact (e.g., obscure administrative classifications) and the evidence only provides names, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- If the claim describes a famous relationship (e.g., an inventor and their alma mater, a film and its award year) and the entities are present, the claim is **SUPPORTED**.

## Output Requirements
- **Reasoning**: Briefly explain your deduction process:
    1. Identify the entities in the claim.
    2. Confirm their presence in the evidence (ignoring values).
    3. State the factual verification based on internal knowledge.
- **Final Verdict**: You **MUST** end your response with a single line containing exactly one of the following labels:
    - `SUPPORTED`
    - `NOT_SUPPORTED`

2. **Fact Check**: Internal knowledge confirms Ermal C. Fraze is the inventor of the pop-top can and attended Kettering University.
3. **Conclusion**: The entities match and the fact is true.

Iteration 8 [k=0]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task: Claim Verification with Strict Entity-Based Evidence

## Objective
Determine whether a given `Claim` is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based **strictly** on the provided `Evidence` list and your internal knowledge base.

## Input Format
- **Evidence**: A list of JSON-like objects in the format `{'key': 'Entity Name', 'value': <number>}`.
- **Claim**: A natural language sentence or paragraph making an assertion about the entities.

## Critical Guidelines for Reasoning

### 1. Interpretation of Evidence Data
- **Ignore Numerical Values**: The `value` field (e.g., 0, 1, 5) is **metadata** (likely confidence scores or indices). **DO NOT** use these numbers for any mathematical comparison or logic.
- **Focus on Entity Presence**: The only relevant information is the **presence of the entity name** (`key`) in the evidence list.

### 2. The "Strict Entity Gatekeeper" Rule (Crucial)
Before applying any internal knowledge, you must perform a **mandatory entity check**:
- **Step 1: Extract All Entities**: Identify every specific named entity (people, songs, albums, organizations, specific titles) explicitly mentioned in the `Claim`.
- **Step 2: Verify Presence**: Check if **EVERY** extracted entity exists as a `key` in the `Evidence` list.
  - **If ANY entity mentioned in the claim is MISSING from the evidence keys**: The claim is immediately **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
  - *Rationale*: The task requires the evidence to support the claim. If the evidence does not contain the specific entity required to prove a part of the claim (e.g., the songwriter "Dallas Frazier" is mentioned in the claim but not in the evidence), the claim cannot be verified using the provided context, even if the fact is true in reality.
  - *Exception*: Generic terms (e.g., "plants", "musician", "album") that describe the category of an entity do not need to be in the evidence keys, provided the specific entity (e.g., "Bellis", "Matt Thiessen") is present.

### 3. Verification Strategy (Context + Knowledge)
Only if **ALL** specific entities are present in the evidence, proceed to Step 3:
- **Fact Verification**: Use your internal knowledge to verify if the relationship or attribute described in the claim is factually true for the confirmed entities.
  - **SUPPORTED**: All entities are present in the evidence AND the claim describes a known, true fact.
  - **NOT_SUPPORTED**: All entities are present, but the claim makes a false assertion (e.g., incorrect authorship, wrong relationship).

### 4. Handling Complex Claims
- If a claim is compound (e.g., "X wrote Y and Y is on Z"), and the evidence contains X, Y, and Z, verify both parts. If either part is false, the verdict is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- If the claim mentions an entity (e.g., "Jon Foreman") to establish a specific relationship (e.g., "co-wrote with"), and that entity is missing from the evidence, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED** due to the "Strict Entity Gatekeeper" Rule.

## Output Requirements
- **Reasoning**: Briefly explain your deduction process:
  1. List the specific entities identified in the claim.
  2. Explicitly state which entities are present in the evidence and which are **missing**.
  3. If any entity is missing, stop and declare **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
  4. If all entities are present, state the factual verification based on internal knowledge.
- **Final Verdict**: You **MUST** end your response with a single line containing exactly one of the following labels:
  - `SUPPORTED`
  - `NOT_SUPPORTED`

## Example Walkthrough
**Input**:
Evidence: `{'key': 'Ain't Living Long Like This', 'value': 3}`, `{'key': 'Fancy Free (The Oak Ridge Boys album)', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': 'An American Dream (song)', 'value': 1}`
Claim: "This song was written by Dallas Frazier and is featured on the third country studio album by the Oak Ridge Boys."

**Deduction**:
1. **Identify Entities**: The claim mentions "Ain't Living Long Like This" (implied by context), "Dallas Frazier", "Oak Ridge Boys", and "Fancy Free" (implied by context).
2. **Confirm Presence in Evidence**:
   - "Ain't Living Long Like This": **Present**.
   - "Fancy Free (The Oak Ridge Boys album)": **Present**.
   - "Dallas Frazier": **NOT PRESENT** in the evidence keys.
   - "Oak Ridge Boys": **NOT PRESENT** as a standalone key (only inside the album title).
3. **Application of Gatekeeper Rule**: Since the specific entity "Dallas Frazier" is explicitly named in the claim but is missing from the evidence list, the claim cannot be verified based on the provided evidence.
4. **Conclusion**: The claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED** due to missing entity evidence, regardless of the factual truth of the songwriting.

**Final Verdict**: NOT_SUPPORTED

Iteration 8 [k=1]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task: Claim Verification with Strict Entity-Based Evidence

## Objective
Determine whether a given `Claim` is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based strictly on the provided `Evidence` list and your internal knowledge base.

## Input Format
- **Evidence**: A list of JSON-like objects in the format `{'key': 'Entity Name', 'value': <number>}`.
- **Claim**: A natural language sentence or paragraph making an assertion about the entities.

## Critical Guidelines for Reasoning

### 1. Interpretation of Evidence Data
- **Ignore Numerical Values**: The `value` field (e.g., 0, 1, 5) is metadata (confidence scores, indices, or noise). **DO NOT** use these numbers for mathematical comparison or logic.
- **Focus on Exact Entity Presence**: The only relevant information is the **exact presence of the entity name** in the `key` field.
  - **Exact Match Required**: An entity is considered "retrieved" ONLY if the string in the claim matches the `key` in the evidence exactly (or is the primary subject of the key).
  - **No Substring Matching**: If a claim mentions "Dallas Frazier" as a writer, but the evidence only contains "Fancy Free (The Oak Ridge Boys album)", the entity "Dallas Frazier" is **NOT** present. You cannot infer the presence of a person from an album title or other entity's name.
  - **No Implicit Inference**: Do not assume an entity is present if it is only mentioned in the claim but missing from the evidence keys.

### 2. Verification Strategy (The "All-or-Nothing" Logic)
This task requires a strict two-step verification process. **If either step fails, the verdict is NOT_SUPPORTED.**

**Step 1: Entity Availability Check (The Gatekeeper)**
- Identify **every** specific entity (Person, Organization, Work, Location, etc.) explicitly mentioned in the claim.
- Check if **each** of these entities exists as a `key` in the `Evidence` list.
- **CRITICAL RULE**: If **any** entity required to substantiate the claim is **missing** from the evidence keys, the claim is immediately **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
  - *Example*: If the claim says "X wrote Y with Z", and evidence contains X and Y but **not** Z, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**, even if X and Y are present and the fact is true.
  - *Example*: If the claim says "A and B are musicians", and evidence contains A but **not** B, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

**Step 2: Fact Verification (The Truth Check)**
- **Only** if **ALL** entities identified in Step 1 are present in the evidence, proceed to this step.
- Use your **internal knowledge** to verify if the relationship or attribute described in the claim is factually true for those specific entities.
  - **SUPPORTED**: All entities are present in evidence AND the claim describes a known, true fact.
  - **NOT_SUPPORTED**: All entities are present, but the claim makes a false assertion (e.g., wrong author, wrong relationship, wrong attribute).

### 3. Handling Compound and Ambiguous Claims
- **Compound Assertions**: If a claim contains multiple distinct assertions (e.g., "X wrote Y, and X is a musician"), **all** parts must be verifiable. If one part relies on a missing entity or is factually false, the entire claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Obscure Attributes**: If the claim relies on a specific attribute (e.g., "third studio album") that is not a standard, well-known fact and the evidence does not explicitly confirm it, treat it as **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

## Output Requirements
- **Reasoning**: Briefly explain your deduction process:
  1. List the specific entities mentioned in the claim.
  2. Explicitly state which entities are **present** and which are **missing** from the evidence keys.
  3. If any entity is missing, stop and conclude **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
  4. If all entities are present, verify the factual accuracy using internal knowledge.
- **Final Verdict**: You **MUST** end your response with a single line containing exactly one of the following labels:
  - `SUPPORTED`
  - `NOT_SUPPORTED`

## Example Walkthroughs

### Example A: Missing Entity (Strict Failure)
**Input**:
Evidence: `{'key': 'Bellis', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': 'Syzygium jambos', 'value': 0}`
Claim: "Both Bellis and Syzygium jambos are plants, and were discovered by John Smith."

**Deduction**:
1. **Entities**: "Bellis", "Syzygium jambos", "John Smith".
2. **Presence Check**:
   - "Bellis": Present.
   - "Syzygium jambos": Present.
   - "John Smith": **NOT Present** in evidence keys.
3. **Conclusion**: Since "John Smith" is missing from the evidence, we cannot verify the claim regarding his discovery. The entity availability check fails.
**Final Verdict**: NOT_SUPPORTED

### Example B: False Fact (Strict Failure)
**Input**:
Evidence: `{'key': 'Matt Thiessen', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': 'George Thorogood', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': 'Rebuild (song)', 'value': 0}`
Claim: "Matt Thiessen and George Thorogood are both musicians who co-wrote Rebuild."

**Deduction**:
1. **Entities**: "Matt Thiessen", "George Thorogood", "Rebuild (song)".
2. **Presence Check**: All three entities are present in the evidence keys.
3. **Fact Check**:
   - Are they musicians? Yes.
   - Did they co-write "Rebuild"? **No**. Internal knowledge confirms Matt Thiessen wrote "Rebuild" alone (or with others, but not George Thorogood).
4. **Conclusion**: Entities are present, but the factual assertion is false.
**Final Verdict**: NOT_SUPPORTED

### Example C: Supported
**Input**:
Evidence: `{'key': 'Kettering University', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': 'Ermal C. Fraze', 'value': 5}`
Claim: "Ermal C. Fraze obtained a degree at Kettering University."

**Deduction**:
1. **Entities**: "Ermal C. Fraze", "Kettering University".
2. **Presence Check**: Both are present in evidence keys.
3. **Fact Check**: Internal knowledge confirms Fraze attended Kettering.
4. **Conclusion**: Entities present and fact is true.
**Final Verdict**: SUPPORTED

Iteration 8 [k=2]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task: Claim Verification with Strict Entity-Based Evidence

## Objective
Determine whether a given `Claim` is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided `Evidence` and your internal knowledge base.

## Input Format
- **Evidence**: A list of JSON-like objects in the format `{'key': 'Entity Name', 'value': <number>}`.
- **Claim**: A natural language sentence or paragraph making an assertion about the entities.

## Critical Guidelines for Reasoning

### 1. Interpretation of Evidence Data
- **Ignore Numerical Values**: The `value` field (e.g., 0, 1, 5) in the evidence objects is **metadata** (likely retrieval confidence scores, indices, or noise). **DO NOT** use these numbers for mathematical comparison or logical deduction.
- **Focus on Entity Presence**: The **only** valid information in the evidence is the **presence of the entity name** (`key`).
  - An entity is considered "verified" **ONLY** if its exact name (or a clear, unambiguous variation) appears as a `key` in the evidence list.
  - **Strict Matching**: If a claim mentions a specific entity (e.g., an author, a specific person, a specific song title) that is **NOT** present in the evidence keys, that specific part of the claim cannot be verified via the provided evidence.

### 2. Verification Strategy (The "Strict Context + Knowledge" Logic)
This task requires a two-step verification process. **Both** steps must pass for a `SUPPORTED` verdict.

**Step 1: Entity Matching (The Gatekeeper)**
- Extract **every** specific entity mentioned in the claim (e.g., people, albums, songs, specific organizations, locations).
- Check if **ALL** of these entities appear in the `Evidence` list keys.
  - **CRITICAL RULE**: If **any** entity essential to the claim's assertion is **missing** from the evidence keys, the claim is immediately **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
  - *Example*: If the claim says "Song X was written by Author Y," and "Song X" is in the evidence but "Author Y" is not, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**, even if your internal knowledge confirms Author Y wrote Song X. The evidence provided is insufficient to support the specific claim structure.
  - *Note on Sub-entities*: If an entity is embedded within another key (e.g., "Oak Ridge Boys" inside "Fancy Free (The Oak Ridge Boys album)"), it is **not** considered a standalone match unless the claim specifically refers to the album title. If the claim refers to the band as a distinct entity, it must appear as a distinct key.

**Step 2: Fact Verification**
- **Only if** all required entities are present in the evidence, proceed to verify the factual accuracy of the relationship or attribute described.
- **Supported**: All entities are present in the evidence AND the claim describes a factually true relationship (e.g., "X is the inventor of Y", "Z is a university").
- **Not Supported**:
  - Any required entity is missing from the evidence (fails Step 1).
  - All entities are present, but the claim makes a **factually false** assertion (e.g., attributing a song to the wrong writer, stating a false relationship between two present entities).
  - The claim relies on obscure attributes that cannot be verified even with the entities present.

### 3. Handling Ambiguity and Falsehoods
- **Missing Entities**: If the claim relies on a specific attribute (e.g., "written by Dallas Frazier") and the entity ("Dallas Frazier") is not in the evidence, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**. Do not use internal knowledge to "fill in the gap" for missing evidence keys.
- **False Relationships**: If the entities are present but the relationship is false (e.g., "Matt Thiessen wrote Rebuild with Jon Foreman" when Jon Foreman did not co-write it), the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Partial Matches**: If a claim lists multiple conditions and one fails (either missing entity or false fact), the entire claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

## Output Requirements
- **Reasoning**: Briefly explain your deduction process:
    1. List the specific entities identified in the claim.
    2. Explicitly state which entities are present in the evidence and which are **missing**.
    3. If any entity is missing, state that the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED** due to insufficient evidence.
    4. If all entities are present, state the factual verification result (True/False).
- **Final Verdict**: You **MUST** end your response with a single line containing exactly one of the following labels:
    - `SUPPORTED`
    - `NOT_SUPPORTED`

## Example Walkthroughs

### Example A: Missing Entity (Strict Rule)
**Input**:
Evidence: `{'key': 'Ain't Living Long Like This', 'value': 3}`, `{'key': 'An American Dream (song)', 'value': 1}`, `{'key': 'Fancy Free (The Oak Ridge Boys album)', 'value': 0}`
Claim: "This song was written by Dallas Frazier and is featured on the third country studio album by the Oak Ridge Boys."

**Deduction**:
1. **Entities**: "Ain't Living Long Like This", "Dallas Frazier", "Oak Ridge Boys".
2. **Presence Check**:
   - "Ain't Living Long Like This": Present.
   - "Fancy Free...": Present (contains album info).
   - "Dallas Frazier": **MISSING** from evidence keys.
   - "Oak Ridge Boys": **MISSING** as a standalone key (only embedded in album title).
3. **Conclusion**: Since the claim explicitly relies on the author "Dallas Frazier" and the band "Oak Ridge Boys" as distinct entities, and these are not present in the evidence keys, the claim cannot be supported by the provided evidence.
**Final Verdict**: NOT_SUPPORTED

### Example B: Factual Error
**Input**:
Evidence: `{'key': 'Matt Thiessen', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': 'George Thorogood', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': 'Rebuild (song)', 'value': 0}`
Claim: "Matt Thiessen wrote Rebuild with Jon Foreman."

**Deduction**:
1. **Entities**: "Matt Thiessen", "Rebuild (song)", "Jon Foreman".
2. **Presence Check**: "Jon Foreman" is **MISSING** from evidence.
3. **Conclusion**: Even if we ignored the missing entity, internal knowledge confirms Jon Foreman did not co-write "Rebuild". The claim is factually false.
**Final Verdict**: NOT_SUPPORTED

### Example C: Full Support
**Input**:
Evidence: `{'key': 'Bellis', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': 'Syzygium jambos', 'value': 0}`
Claim: "Both Bellis and Syzygium jambos are plants."

**Deduction**:
1. **Entities**: "Bellis", "Syzygium jambos".
2. **Presence Check**: Both are present in evidence keys.
3. **Fact Check**: Internal knowledge confirms both are plant genera/species.
4. **Conclusion**: Entities present and fact is true.
**Final Verdict**: SUPPORTED

Iteration 9 [k=0]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task: Claim Verification with Entity-Based Evidence

## Objective
Determine whether a given `Claim` is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided `Evidence` and your internal knowledge base.

## Input Format
- **Evidence**: A list of JSON-like objects in the format `{'key': 'Entity Name', 'value': <number>}`.
- **Claim**: A natural language sentence or paragraph making an assertion about the entities.

## Critical Guidelines for Reasoning

### 1. Interpretation of Evidence Data
- **Ignore Numerical Values**: The `value` field (e.g., 0, 1, 5) in the evidence objects is **metadata** (likely retrieval confidence scores, indices, or noise). **DO NOT** use these numbers for mathematical comparison or as part of the fact-checking logic.
- **Focus on Entity Presence**: The only relevant information in the evidence is the **presence of the entity name** (`key`). If an entity mentioned in the claim appears in the evidence list, it is considered "retrieved" and valid for verification.

### 2. Verification Strategy (The "Context + Knowledge" Logic)
This task requires a strict two-step verification process. **Both steps must pass for a claim to be SUPPORTED.**

**Step 1: Entity Matching**
- Identify the specific entities (people, places, events, organizations, species) required to prove the claim.
- Check if these specific entities appear as `key` values in the `Evidence` list.
- *Note*: If a claim refers to an entity by description (e.g., "the three-time defending champion"), you must use your internal knowledge to resolve that description to a specific name (e.g., "Marc Rosset") and then check if that name exists in the evidence.
- **Failure Condition**: If any critical entity required to verify the claim is missing from the evidence keys, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

**Step 2: Fact Verification (Crucial)**
- Once entities are confirmed present, use your **internal knowledge** to verify if the **specific relationship, attribute, or event** described in the claim is factually true.
- **SUPPORTED**: The entities are present in the evidence AND the claim describes a known, true fact about them (e.g., "X is the inventor of Y", "Z is a university", "A won the tournament in 1994").
- **NOT_SUPPORTED**: The entities are present, but the claim makes an assertion that is **false**, **inaccurate**, or **contradicts historical records**.
    - *Example of False Assertion*: If the evidence contains "Riccardo Cocchi" and "Yulia Zagoruychenko", but the claim says "Riccardo Cocchi is Ukrainian," the verdict is **NOT_SUPPORTED** because the nationality attribute is false, even though the names are present.
    - *Example of False Relationship*: If the evidence contains "Marc Rosset" and "1994 Waldbaum's Cup", but the claim falsely states he was the "three-time defending champion who lost" (when he was actually the defending champion but the specific count or outcome is wrong), the verdict is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
    - *Example of Obscurity*: If the claim relies on a specific attribute that is not a well-known, verifiable fact (e.g., obscure administrative classifications) and the evidence only provides names, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### 3. Handling Ambiguity and "Trick" Claims
- **Strict Truth Standard**: Do not assume a claim is true just because the entities are real and present. You must verify the *entirety* of the assertion.
- **Negative Verification**: If you know the claim is false based on internal knowledge, you must output **NOT_SUPPORTED**, regardless of how many entities are found in the evidence.
- **Incomplete Evidence**: If the claim implies a connection between two entities, but the evidence only lists the entities separately without context, and you cannot verify the connection via internal knowledge, output **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

## Output Requirements
- **Reasoning**: Briefly explain your deduction process:
    1.  **Entity Identification**: List the entities in the claim and confirm their presence in the evidence keys (explicitly stating that numerical values are ignored).
    2.  **Fact Check**: State the factual verification based on internal knowledge. Explicitly identify if any part of the claim (nationality, role, date, relationship) is factually incorrect.
    3.  **Conclusion**: Summarize why the claim is supported or not supported based on the combination of evidence presence and factual accuracy.
- **Final Verdict**: You **MUST** end your response with a single line containing exactly one of the following labels:
    - `SUPPORTED`
    - `NOT_SUPPORTED`

**WARNING**: Failure to provide the final verdict line in the exact format specified will result in the response being considered invalid.

## Example Walkthrough
**Input**:
Evidence: `{'key': 'Kettering University', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': 'Ermal C. Fraze', 'value': 5}`
Claim: "Ermal C. Fraze obtained a degree at Kettering University."

**Deduction**:
1. **Entities**: "Ermal C. Fraze" and "Kettering University" are present in the evidence keys. (Values 0 and 5 are ignored).
2. **Fact Check**: Internal knowledge confirms Ermal C. Fraze is the inventor of the pop-top can and attended Kettering University. The relationship is true.
3. **Conclusion**: The entities match and the fact is true.

**Final Verdict**: SUPPORTED

**Counter-Example (False Attribute)**:
Evidence: `{'key': 'Riccardo Cocchi', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': 'Yulia Zagoruychenko', 'value': 0}`
Claim: "Ukrainian choreographer Riccardo Cocchi is Yulia Zagoruychenko's dance partner."

**Deduction**:
1. **Entities**: "Riccardo Cocchi" and "Yulia Zagoruychenko" are present in the evidence keys.
2. **Fact Check**: Internal knowledge confirms Riccardo Cocchi is **Italian**, not Ukrainian. While they were dance partners, the attribute "Ukrainian" is factually false.
3. **Conclusion**: The claim contains a false assertion regarding nationality.
**Final Verdict**: NOT_SUPPORTED
Iteration 9 [k=0]: Candidate score sum = 1.0 (best so far = -inf)
Iteration 9 [k=1]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task: Strict Evidence-Based Claim Verification

## Objective
Determine whether a given `Claim` is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based **strictly** on the provided `Evidence`.

## Input Format
- **Evidence**: A list of JSON-like objects in the format `{'key': 'Entity Name', 'value': <number>}`.
- **Claim**: A natural language sentence or paragraph making an assertion about the entities.

## Critical Guidelines for Reasoning

### 1. Interpretation of Evidence Data
- **Ignore Numerical Values**: The `value` field (e.g., 0, 1, 5) in the evidence objects is **metadata** (likely retrieval confidence scores, indices, or noise). **DO NOT** use these numbers for mathematical comparison or logic.
- **Focus on Entity Presence**: The `key` field represents the only valid data. An entity is considered "retrieved" if its name appears exactly (or with high semantic similarity) in the `key` field of the evidence list.

### 2. Verification Strategy (The "Strict Evidence" Logic)
**CRITICAL UPDATE**: You must **NOT** use your internal knowledge base to verify the truthfulness of the claim's specific assertions (e.g., "X is the inventor of Y", "X is a professional tennis player", "X was born in Y").

The verification process is strictly binary:
1.  **Entity Matching**: Identify all specific entities, attributes, or relationships mentioned in the `Claim`.
2.  **Evidence Check**: Check if the **specific fact** asserted in the claim is explicitly present in the `Evidence` keys.
    - **SUPPORTED**: The claim is supported **ONLY IF** the evidence keys explicitly contain the specific relationship or attribute described. (Note: In the current input format, evidence usually only contains entity names. If the claim asserts a relationship *between* entities or an *attribute* of an entity that is not explicitly listed as a separate key or a combined phrase in the evidence, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**).
    - **NOT_SUPPORTED**: If the evidence only lists the *names* of the entities involved, but does not explicitly confirm the *relationship* or *attribute* described in the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**, even if the statement is factually true in the real world.

### 3. Handling Ambiguity and "True" Facts
- **The "True but Unproven" Rule**: If a claim is factually true in the real world (e.g., "Marc Rosset is a professional tennis player") but the provided evidence only lists the name "Marc Rosset" without the phrase "professional tennis player" or a context that proves it, you **MUST** label it **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Attribute Mismatch**: If the claim assigns a specific attribute (e.g., "Ukrainian choreographer") to an entity, and the evidence only lists the entity name, you cannot verify the attribute. If the attribute is false (as per internal knowledge) OR if the attribute is true but not in evidence, the result is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Complex Claims**: For claims involving multiple steps (e.g., "The person who won X is also Y"), if the evidence does not explicitly link "Winner of X" to "Y" in a single key or a clear chain of keys, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

## Output Requirements
- **Reasoning**: Briefly explain your deduction process:
    1. Identify the specific entities and the **specific assertion/relationship** made in the claim.
    2. List the relevant entities found in the `Evidence` keys.
    3. **Crucial Step**: Explicitly state whether the **specific assertion** (the relationship or attribute) is found in the evidence keys.
        - If the evidence only contains the entity names but not the relationship: State that the evidence confirms the entities exist but **fails to confirm the specific relationship/attribute**.
        - If the evidence does not contain the entity: State the entity is missing.
    4. Conclude based **solely** on the presence of the evidence for the specific claim.
- **Final Verdict**: You **MUST** end your response with a single line containing exactly one of the following labels:
    - `SUPPORTED`
    - `NOT_SUPPORTED`

## Example Walkthrough (Corrected Logic)

**Input**:
Evidence: `{'key': 'Marc Rosset', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': '1994 Waldbaum's Hamlet Cup – Singles', 'value': 0}`
Claim: "The three time defending champion who lost the Singles title at the 1994 Waldbaum's Hamlet Cup has been a professional tennis player."

**Deduction**:
1.  **Entities & Assertion**: The claim identifies "Marc Rosset" (implied by the description) and asserts the attribute: "is a professional tennis player".
2.  **Entity Matching**: "Marc Rosset" is present in the evidence keys. "1994 Waldbaum's Hamlet Cup – Singles" is present.

Iteration 9 [k=2]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task: Claim Verification with Entity-Based Evidence

## Objective
Determine whether a given `Claim` is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided `Evidence` and your internal knowledge base.

## Input Format
- **Evidence**: A list of JSON-like objects in the format `{'key': 'Entity Name', 'value': <number>}`.
- **Claim**: A natural language sentence or paragraph making an assertion about entities.

## Critical Guidelines for Reasoning

### 1. Interpretation of Evidence Data
- **Strictly Ignore Numerical Values**: The `value` field (e.g., 0, 1, 5) is metadata (confidence scores, indices, or noise). **DO NOT** use these numbers for any comparison or logic.
- **Focus on Entity Presence**: The only valid data in the evidence is the **`key` (Entity Name)**. An entity is considered "retrieved" only if its exact name appears as a `key` in the evidence list.

### 2. Verification Strategy (The "Resolution + Fact" Logic)
This task requires a three-step verification process:

#### Step 1: Entity Resolution (Crucial)
The claim may refer to entities using **descriptions** rather than explicit names (e.g., "The three-time defending champion who lost in 1994").
- **Action**: Use your internal knowledge to resolve the description to the **specific entity name** (e.g., "Marc Rosset").
- **Check**: Verify if this **resolved name** exists as a `key` in the `Evidence` list.
- **Failure Condition**: If the resolved name is **not** present in the evidence keys, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**, regardless of whether the description is factually true in the real world. The evidence must explicitly contain the entity required to prove the claim.

#### Step 2: Entity Matching
- If the claim mentions entities explicitly (e.g., "Riccardo Cocchi"), check if they appear in the evidence keys.
- If the claim mentions entities implicitly (via description), ensure the **resolved name** from Step 1 appears in the evidence keys.

#### Step 3: Fact Verification
Once all necessary entities are confirmed present in the evidence:
- **Attribute Check**: Verify if the specific attributes or relationships described in the claim are factually true for those entities (e.g., Is Riccardo Cocchi Ukrainian? No, he is Italian).
- **Knowledge Scope Check**:
  - If the fact is a well-known, verifiable standard (e.g., "X is the inventor of Y", "Z is a professional tennis player"), and the entities are present, the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
  - If the fact relies on obscure, niche, or highly specific administrative/historical details (e.g., "introduced in 1902 to control genus X") that are not common knowledge, or if the logical connection is ambiguous, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### 3. Decision Rules Summary
- **SUPPORTED**: 
  1. All entities (explicit or resolved) are present in the evidence keys.
  2. The claim's assertions about these entities are factually correct and verifiable.
- **NOT_SUPPORTED**: 
  1. Any required entity (explicit or resolved) is **missing** from the evidence keys.
  2. Any required entity is present, but the claim contains a **false attribute** (e.g., wrong nationality, wrong role).
  3. The claim relies on obscure facts that cannot be confidently verified as standard knowledge.

## Output Requirements
- **Reasoning**: Briefly explain your deduction process:
  1. Identify entities (explicit or resolved via internal knowledge).
  2. Confirm their presence in the evidence keys (ignoring values).
  3. State the factual verification based on internal knowledge (checking for false attributes or obscurity).
- **Final Verdict**: You **MUST** end your response with a single line containing exactly one of the following labels:
  - `SUPPORTED`
  - `NOT_SUPPORTED`

## Example Walkthroughs

### Example A (Implicit Entity Missing)
**Input**:
Evidence: `{'key': 'Marc Rosset', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': 'Max Mirnyi', 'value': 0}`
Claim: "The three time defending champion who lost the Singles title at the 1994 Waldbaum's Hamlet Cup has been a professional tennis player."

**Deduction**:
1. **Resolution**: Internal knowledge identifies "The three time defending champion who lost... 1994" as **Marc Rosset**.
2. **Matching**: "Marc Rosset" is present in the evidence keys.
3. **Fact Check**: Marc Rosset is a professional tennis player.
4. **Conclusion**: Entities match and fact is true.
**Final Verdict**: SUPPORTED

*(Note: If the evidence had NOT included 'Marc Rosset', the verdict would be NOT_SUPPORTED because the evidence failed to retrieve the resolved entity.)*

### Example B (False Attribute)
**Input**:
Evidence: `{'key': 'Riccardo Cocchi', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': 'Yulia Zagoruychenko', 'value': 0}`
Claim: "Ukrainian choreographer Riccardo Cocchi is Yulia Zagoruychenko's dance partner."

**Deduction**:
1. **Matching**: Both "Riccardo Cocchi" and "Yulia Zagoruychenko" are present in evidence keys.
2. **Fact Check**: While they are dance partners, internal knowledge confirms Riccardo Cocchi is **Italian**, not Ukrainian.
3. **Conclusion**: The claim contains a false attribute.
**Final Verdict**: NOT_SUPPORTED

### Example C (Obscure/Unverifiable Fact)
**Input**:
Evidence: `{'key': 'Lantana', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': 'Strymon bazochii', 'value': 2}`
Claim: "Strymon bazochii was introduced to Hawaii in 1902 to control the genus Lantana."

**Deduction**:
1. **Matching**: "Strymon bazochii" and "Lantana" are present in evidence keys.
2. **Fact Check**: While *Strymon bazochii* is a butterfly and *Lantana* is a plant, the specific historical claim that this specific butterfly was introduced in 1902 for this specific purpose is an obscure, likely incorrect, or unverifiable detail not supported by standard general knowledge.
3. **Conclusion**: The claim relies on an obscure/unverifiable attribute.
**Final Verdict**: NOT_SUPPORTED
